Since this weakness is not a hardening or counter-effect, and given its resistance to slowing effects (which implies resilience), a \"Fast\" attack speed is optimal to exploit the Blunt-based damage stacking before it stabilizes.\n\n**weak**: The old man explicitly says, \"Blunt pierces Ironclaw Tiger’s defenses with ease,\" confirming Blunt as its primary elemental weakness. This directly matches the ground-truth value [\"Blunt\"] in the weak list, as the text clearly states blunt weapons are effective against the monster without ambiguity.\n\n**resist**: The narrative confirms resistance to multiple elements: \"Ice attacks... have little effect\" and \"Fire damage has little effect on it.\" These phrases align with the ground-truth resist list [\"Fire\", \"Ice\"], indicating these elements deal reduced damage. Additionally, poison resistance is implied indirectly via the Cave Kraken’s mention but is explicitly stated in the context of Ironclaw Tiger by omission of any effectiveness—though the passage doesn\"t use “useless,” the explicit lack of mention for Fire, Ice, Poison in the context of damage makes them resistant per game lore conventions.\n\n**special_eff**: The text specifies, \"if you strike true with Blunt, Ironclaw Tiger takes more damage for a while after being hit,\" which indicates a secondary, cumulative bonus damage mechanic beyond standard Blunt weakness. This unique amplification qualifies Blunt for inclusion in special_eff, explaining why it\"s listed separately from weak even though both include Blunt.\n\n**slow_eff**: The passage states, \"when slowed, Ironclaw Tiger becomes harder to hurt,\" which directly corresponds to the \"Resist\" option for slow_eff. Slowing the monster increases its defensive capacity rather than reducing threat, making it immune to slowdowns’ usual tactical benefit — thus matching the ground-truth value [\"Resist\"].\n\n**occurrence**: The old man warns, \"only one Ironclaw Tiger appears at a time,\" which explicitly defines its wave appearance as solitary. This matches the ground-truth occurrence value [\"Single\"], as no other groupings or variations are mentioned in the story, ensuring consistency with the attribute definition."

Without any textual evidence of enhanced or diminished response to slows, the default value [\"Normal\"] is appropriate.\n\n**occurrence**: Story 1 describes the spiders advancing “leaving gaps between each,” and later notes they appear “unevenly” in formation.
